Japanese Goods Smuggled in Disguise

After the boycott, the Japanese transported seafood from Shanghai to Dalian and Yantai, repackaged it, and then passed it off as Chinese fish. It has been confirmed that a considerable amount has already been transported. It has recently been discovered that unscrupulous merchants are packaging it for them. It is also heard that a batch of Japanese yarn in this port was transported by Japanese ships to a warehouse in the Japanese concession in Tianjin, where the brand name and appearance were changed. Then it was transported by the Pinghan train to Hankou and then on to Sichuan. The first batch of this smuggled Japanese yarn has already been shipped from Shanghai.

Inspection of Japanese Goods at Yuanda and Other Hardware Stores Triggers a Disturbance

▲ Zhu Lide Assaults Inspector ▲ Falsely Reports to the Police Claiming Robbery

Recently, Yuanda, Yuyu, Xinyuyu and other hardware stores on Zhejiang Road in this port have been selling large quantities of Japanese goods. The Anti-Japanese Association, upon receiving a report, together with the inspection team of the hardware industry association, went to inspect on the 3rd. However, Zhu Lide, the son-in-law of the store owner (a postal worker at the post office), dared to punch an inspector. On the 7th, when the inspectors continued their inspection, he falsely reported to the police, resulting in the arrest of six inspectors. Upon receiving this report, the Anti-Japanese Association was extremely indignant. Yesterday, the standing committee resolved to confiscate the goods, continue to investigate and confiscate any un-confiscated goods, and then decide on how to deal with the matter. The details of the case are recorded below: (Report from the Inspection Department) Regarding the report, the department instructed Captain Yang Haichang of the special inspection team on the 3rd to go with the hardware industry association to inspect the Japanese goods at Yuyu, Yuanda, Xinyuyu and other hardware stores on Xiamen Road and Zhejiang Road. According to the officer's report, after receiving instructions to investigate and confiscate Japanese goods from Yuyu Hardware, Ge Yunting was instructed on the 3rd to go with inspectors from the hardware industry association to the old store on Xiamen Road to search the residential wing, where a large amount of Japanese goods was found. The next day, the new store on Zhejiang Road was also found to have Japanese goods. While loading the goods onto trucks, Zhu Lide, the son-in-law of the store owner, forcibly obstructed them and even dared to punch the inspector from the hardware industry association. The standing committee mediated the next day, and he apologized in the newspaper. The goods that had not been loaded were taken by the officer again on the morning of the 5th. Zhang, a store employee, said that the store had sent a letter to the hardware industry association for registration, but the association did not allow it because they were not members, resulting in a deadlock. The officer was invited to the association to negotiate for a one-day extension. The officer was not in a position to decide, so he invited Zhang to the department for instructions. Chief Hu allowed the request and set a one-day deadline. Unexpectedly, no letter from the hardware industry association had been received by noon today, and no one from the store came to negotiate. At 1:30, the officer led team members Song Peiji, Xiao Dingrong, Lou Qinghe, Li Changhui, and Lu Jinsheng of the detective department to load the goods. Unexpectedly, Zhu Lide, the son-in-law of the store owner, secretly falsely reported to the police, claiming that a large number of robbers were looting goods worth more than 10,000 yuan from the store. Suddenly, a large team of detectives rushed over, arrested the officer and five other people from the detective department without asking questions, and took them to the police station. Later, the association sent someone to bail them out, which took three hours before they were released. It is thought that Yuyu's Japanese goods were not registered in advance, nor were any procedures gone through with the hardware industry association. They were displayed and sold in the front, and hidden in the residence in secret. Such reckless behavior has already been abandoned by the Chinese people. Moreover, they dared to report to the police and frame them in order to vent their anger. Although they were willing to sacrifice for the love of the country, the association's prestige and the future of the inspection should be taken into account, and what should be done to properly handle the aftermath. If various industries follow suit, the anti-Japanese work will be unimaginable. They are specifically reporting in detail, and they are asking for a decision to be made to deal with the matter properly. They also report that the police have warned them that in the future, they must report to the police and obtain permission before loading goods in the concession, otherwise, once the store reports, they will be punished for violating the law and will not be spared again. Based on this, it is clear that Yuanda Hardware's Japanese goods were neither registered with the association nor were any procedures gone through with the association. It is obvious that they are seeking profit by selling privately. The inspectors are acting correctly in loading the goods. However, the store owner dared to instigate Zhu Lide to fabricate a false report to the police and have the inspectors arrested. If such crazy people are not severely punished, the inspectors' work will have no protection, and the association's prestige will be completely swept away. The previous report is specifically presented to the council, and they ask for prompt review, strict punishment, so as to warn the evil and prevent imitation, which is in the public interest. Respectfully presented to the standing committee, Chen Peide, director of the inspection department, and Zheng Chengqing, deputy director.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Asks the Anti-Japanese Association Not to Arbitrarily Detain Employees

▲ Promote Anti-Japanese Work ▲ Maintain the Livelihood of Employees

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter yesterday to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, stating: With regards, on the 7th of this month, according to a joint letter from the guilds of the cotton industry, paper industry, electrical appliance industry, sugar industry, seafood and sundries industry, yarn industry, seafood business, silk and satin industry, mercerized cotton weaving industry, north-south goods exchange industry, south goods industry, knitting industry, refining industry, department store industry, and new drug industry, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association has often detained low-level employees of various factories and shops during inspections of Japanese goods, and after detaining them, they do not quickly dispose of them, sometimes exceeding ten days without being released. It is not known that low-level employees only follow the instructions of the persons in charge of each factory and shop, and are never allowed to participate in important matters. Therefore, even if each factory and shop does have circumstances of selling Japanese goods, it has nothing to do with these low-level employees. Once they are arbitrarily detained, how can they be treated fairly, resulting in all current employees being in constant fear, which greatly affects commerce. Although it is said that the matter concerns national salvation and cannot be restricted by normal rules, it should also be planned and considered comprehensively to avoid punishing the innocent. Our chamber and other organizations have a duty to do so, and cannot remain silent. In order to protect the reputation of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, it is necessary to make some suggestions. We jointly request your association to check the following principles: (1) Detaining traitors must be done in conjunction with the inspection team of each industry association. Detention should not be used unless there are serious circumstances, solid evidence, and no other means of restraint other than detention. (2) Detention should be limited to the principals of each factory and shop. (3) After detention, the standing committee should be convened within 24 hours to decide on punishment or release. (4) If there are any cases of wrongful detention, the responsible personnel should be severely punished. Please forward this letter to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association for implementation, so as to correct the situation and emphasize human rights. We also hope to hear back from you. In view of this, the handling of Japanese goods by factories and shops has no direct relationship with the low-level employees themselves. If employees are detained because of improper measures taken by the store, it is unreasonable and innocent. It is also easy to cause concern among other employees. The four proposals made by the association and other organizations are aimed at promoting anti-Japanese work and maintaining the lives of employees. Accordingly, we are sending this letter to your association for review and handling, and we hope to hear back from you.

The Great Alliance Committee for Promoting National Products

▲ Representatives' Conference Today ▲ Declaration Issued Yesterday

The Great Alliance Committee for Promoting National Products, in accordance with the resolution of the fourth meeting, in order to resolve disputes in national product factories, ensure the sales of national products, and prepare for national product tea parties, etc., specifically scheduled a National Product Four Groups Factory Member Representatives' Conference at 2:00 PM today (the 10th) on the second floor of the China National Product Maintenance Association at Nine Acres to discuss the implementation methods and to discuss and issue the following declaration: Our association is the general group of the China National Product Maintenance Association, the Shanghai National Product Factories Association, the Shanghai Machine-made National Product Factories Association, and the Shanghai Citizens' Association for Promoting National Products. Its main purpose is to concentrate strength, unite spirits, promote national products, study raw materials, revitalize industry, and develop the economy. Therefore, the position of our association is to work hard with comrades for national products, jointly seek the progress of the enterprise, increase the strength of national product factories, and bear the important mission of promoting national production and saving the country. At this time, when violent Japan is rampant, swallowing the Northeast, and internal and external troubles are coming together, the responsibility of our association is even greater, and the work of our association is even more arduous. We state the main points to the people of the country: (1) Our association recognizes that the shortcut to anti-Japanese resistance is economic severance, and that thoroughly boycotting Japanese goods is the fundamental method of economic severance. Therefore, within the proper bounds, our association is willing to exert all its strength and swear to deal with the anti-Japanese work. (2) If you want to achieve the effect of boycotting Japanese goods, you must support the development of production agencies. This time, the Northeast tragedy has aroused the anger of the whole country, and the only ambition is not to use Japanese goods. However, before the tragedy occurred, each factory had to compromise in order to demand raw materials. Three steps should be distinguished: A. Japanese raw materials imported before the establishment of the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Association will of course not be subject to any punishment. B. Those who implemented the collection of industrial and commercial funds after the establishment of the Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Association can be divided into four categories: (1) those who have registered before the collection of funds, (2) those who have not registered before the collection of funds, (3) those who have collected funds but have not paid, and (4) those who have collected funds and have already paid. C. Those who were established after the establishment of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association should be given a fair criticism based on the circumstances. All those who are not traitors and have justifiable reasons should be exempted from punishment in order to maintain the only factories and support their development, so as to seek self-sufficiency in raw materials. If they are not investigated and punished in the name of traitors, it will not only fail to achieve the effect of anti-Japanese and national salvation, but will also hinder the development of national products. Unsound factories are certainly attacked and closed. That is, the six national product factories that were standardized by the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce have been identified as Japanese goods because they used some old Japanese raw materials, and five of them have been removed. Then, those that are needed daily are not available in national products, and they are turned to European and American imported products. Isn't it heartbreaking? The effectiveness of punishing and creating violent Japan has not yet been greatly achieved, but the pain of factories is inevitable. According to the original intention of anti-Japanese national salvation, they have deviated from each other. Therefore, our association today only has to make a fundamental relief, seek self-sufficiency in raw materials, grit our teeth, and work hard to produce, doing one point to receive one point of effect, and doing one inch to receive one inch of work, in order to go to the path of industrial and national salvation. All those who take illegal actions that undermine or harm the progress of the national product business, the members of our association will take orderly steps and vow to seek a common confrontation. Increasing the strength of the national product industry is to protect the vitality of the country. If all the comrades in the national product industry of our country are fully mobilized, there will be small achievements in May and great achievements in five years. How can it not be easy to avenge and avenge? (3) Our association has the sacred duty to develop production and promote national products, and is determined to serve with great effort and have a widespread impact. We should use our full strength to promote extensively, arouse public attention, enable producers to have the ability to supply as much as possible, and consumers to have the determination to use national products as much as possible, and cooperate with each other to achieve the purpose of anti-Japanese national salvation. (4) The development of national products is first in talent and economy. Therefore, the current work lies in concentrating the talent and economy of the whole country to establish a foundation for planting production and increase the strength of the national product industry. Our association will proceed in accordance with these four principles, with full strength and consistent action. Everyone working hard on the economic battlefield is the key to defeating violent Japan. Enthusiastic comrades are willing to encourage each other.

Japan's Foreign Trade in October

▲ Surplus of 8 Million Yuan Against China

The Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office announced that Japan's total export value in October was 97 million Japanese yen, with a surplus of 20 million yen. However, the trade statistics for the first ten months of this year still show a deficit of 55 million yen, but this is a decrease of 9 million yen compared to the same period last year. In addition, the export value to China in October was 22 million yen, resulting in a surplus of 8 million yen (from China's perspective, it is a deficit). The trade results with China for the first ten months of this year show a total surplus of 36 million yen, but this is a decrease of 34 million yen compared to the same period last year. Furthermore, according to the export value of Japan to China in September, which was 26 million yen, there was also a surplus of 13 million yen.

Ministry of Industry Responds to Municipal Government Regarding Extending Workers' Working Hour Standards

▲Four Restrictions on Extension to Ten Hours

▲Does Not Apply If Labor and Management Agree

Since the implementation of the Factory Law, the issue of factory workers' working hours has been most prone to disputes. In fact, due to various reasons, employers also feel the difficulty of implementing the law. It is heard that the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau previously drafted fifteen items for reviewing the standards of factory workers' working hours and submitted them to the Municipal Government for transfer to the Ministry of Industry for review and handling. Now, the Ministry of Industry has announced the original text of its response to the Municipal Government as follows: For the matter of response, it is approved that the Honorable Municipal Government inquired, according to the report of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, for the matter of requesting instructions. Since the implementation of the Factory Law, regarding the regulation of eight hours of work per day for adult workers, both labor and management have their own reasons, and have requested extensions or reductions. Although there are restrictions on local conditions and the nature of work according to the law, they are too broad and prone to disputes. Therefore, it was resolved at the 97th Bureau Affairs Meeting of this Bureau to review five standards for factory workers' working hours: (1) industries with international competition; (2) emerging industries; (3) industries with operational risks; (4) jobs that do not harm health; (5) extensions agreed upon by both labor and management. Only those that meet one of the above standards shall be allowed to extend working hours to ten hours per day, but the factory shall still be ordered to properly plan reduction methods within two years, to reach eight hours. Whether the proposal is appropriate should be prepared in writing and submitted, requesting your superior to review and instruct accordingly. Based on this, upon investigation, the five standards proposed by the Bureau for reviewing factory workers' working hours are related to the applicable laws and regulations, and should be inquired about for inspection and prompt reply, so as to instruct compliance, etc. Upon investigation, the first, second, and third items of the five standards proposed by the Bureau are still feasible. The fourth item should be corrected to "work that is light and does not harm health." The fifth item does not comply with Article 8 of the Factory Law and should not be approved for application. As for the original report stating that the factory should be ordered to properly plan reduction methods within two years to reach eight hours, according to the extension of working hours, it should be limited to cases where there is a necessary situation. If there is no necessary situation within a shorter period, it should be terminated at any time. Setting a uniform provision of two years would be inflexible and seems inappropriate. Approval is given for the previous inquiry. A corresponding response is made for inspection and instruction. This is addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Government.

The Coffin of Ma Su is Transported to Shanghai for Burial

Mr. Ma Su, who once served as a diplomatic commissioner to the United States and a senior advisor to the Northeast Frontier Defense Headquarters, served the Party and the country for many years, which led to illness from overwork. He passed away at his residence in Beiping on April 4th of this year, and the whole country mourned. Mr. Ma's coffin was moved to Long'an Zen Temple in the eastern city of Beiping for temporary placement. It is now being transported to Shanghai by Mr. Ma's wife, and has been placed in the grand hall of the International Cemetery on Hongqiao Road. A memorial service will be held on November 15th, and he will be buried on the same day. Currently, Mr. Ma's wife resides at 346 Jin Shenfu Road, Shanghai, which is Mr. Ma's funeral arrangement office in Shanghai.

Statement from the Shanghai Publishing Industry Union's Commercial Press Office

The Shanghai Publishing Industry Union's Commercial Press Office, due to reports on the 8th of this month claiming the use of the name "Representatives of All Employees of the Commercial Press" and reports on the 9th claiming the names "Commercial Union, Commercial General Affairs Union," etc., to meet with peace conference representatives Wang, Wu, Cai, and others, specially issued the following statement yesterday (omitted above). The origin of this office and the political stance and propositions of the publishing industry union are briefly disclosed, hoping that people in society will pay attention. (1) The Origin of the Shanghai Publishing Industry Union's Commercial Press Office. The Commercial Press has approximately 4,000 employees in its four major departments in Shanghai: the printing plant, distribution office, general affairs department, and translation department. In 1925, the Printing Union, Distribution Office Employees' Union, General Affairs Department Association, and Translation Department Association were established separately. In 1927, when the Revolutionary Army arrived in Shanghai and the Union Unification Committee was formed, they were renamed the First Branch of the Commercial Press Union, the Third Branch of the Commercial Press Union, the Second Branch of the Commercial Press Union, and the Fourth Branch of the Commercial Press Union. In 1928, when the Second Central Committee established a Union Reorganization Committee, they were renamed the Commercial Press Union, the Commercial Press Distribution Office Employees' Union, the Commercial Press General Affairs Department Employees' Union, and the Commercial Press Translation Department Employees' Union. On February 28th of this year, they were reorganized into the Shanghai Publishing Industry Union's Commercial Press Office, which governs all employees in the four major departments of printing, distribution, general affairs, and editing. Its powers are purely internal. As for all external matters, the entire name of the publishing industry union is responsible for representation. This is because the publishing industry union has five offices under its jurisdiction, including this office, the China Book Company Office, and the World Book Company Office, with a total of more than 5,000 members. (2) The Political Position and Propositions of the Publishing Industry Union. The political stance of the publishing industry union can be found in the founding declaration, in the section on political aspects, excerpted as follows: "To seek the true liberation of the working masses, we must wait for the realization of true democratic politics. To seek the realization of true democratic politics, we must first seek the political status of the working masses. Because the emotions of the workers' revolution are the most intense, their power to promote politics is also the greatest. Politics is driven by revolutionary forces, not only is there no fear of regression, but there is also hope for progress. That is, our current urgent needs, such as (1) freedom of assembly, association, speech, and publication, (2) the right to strike, (3) the right to vote and participate in politics, (4) the right to local autonomy, (5) the establishment of all other civil rights, etc., can only be thoroughly implemented and realized after the working masses have acquired political status. Then, people of all classes can enjoy equal political power in politics, and the embryo of true democratic politics can be formed, and even completely established, to achieve consolidation. This is not only the hope of the workers in this industry, but also the aspiration of workers in all industries in the city and the country. Therefore, what we want to obtain political status is for the masses, not for individuals. Violating this principle, everything is false. Departing from this spirit, even if we run around and shout, we can only exhaust our ability to shout, and there is no benefit to actual benefit. Their recent political propositions can also be found in the 'Declaration to Promote Peaceful Unification Conference' jointly issued by the Publishing Industry Union and various unions in this city, published in the Shen Xin and Xin Shen newspapers on October 30th of this year (not listed separately). It can be seen that the association is striving for democratic political efforts. (omitted below)

Minutes of the Autumn General Meeting of the Medical Association

The Shanghai Medical Association held its autumn general meeting yesterday. More than 150 members attended. Chairman Song Guobin presided over the meeting, and everyone performed the ceremony. First, the chairman reported, followed by reports from Zhou Junchang and Tang Shouxian. Then, proposals were discussed, and the following resolutions were made: (1) Song Guobin proposed to amend Articles 10, 12, 13, and 14 of the association's charter to facilitate handling affairs. Resolution: No need to amend. (2) The Executive Committee proposed to increase membership fees and dues to fund the construction of the association's clubhouse. Resolution: The construction of the association's clubhouse is approved in principle. The construction funds should be planned in detail by the next Executive Committee, and a budget should be prepared and submitted for reporting at the spring general meeting next year. A method for raising funds was also decided. As for increasing membership fees and dues, which involves amending the association's charter, it must also be submitted for discussion at the spring general meeting next year. (3) The Executive Committee proposed to elect representatives to attend the Second National Congress of the National Medical Association and solicit proposals from the general meeting. Resolution: The representatives to attend will be solicited by the next Executive Committee. The proposals for the general meeting will be submitted directly by the members to the next Executive Committee for discussion and submission. (4) Ding Huikang proposed that members of the association should abide by the Physician's Oath and not attack each other. (5) Ye Zhisheng proposed that members who do not abide by the association's Physician's Oath should be punished. The above two proposals are of the same nature and were discussed together. Resolution: Handed over to the next Supervisory Committee to implement its powers in accordance with item C of Article 6 of the association's charter, and handled by the next Executive Committee in accordance with Article 6 of the association's charter. (6) Ye Zhisheng proposed to create a national medicine manufacturing project. Resolution: Approved in principle. The method will be discussed and handled by the next Executive Committee. (7) Song Guobin and Zhu Qiluo proposed to never use Japanese-made medical supplies and add them to the Physician's Oath for permanent compliance. Resolution: Passed. The word "Japanese" will be changed to "enemy" and added to item A of the oath. (8) Hua Jingshuang proposed to supplement the Physician's Oath. Resolution: Whether there is a need to supplement or amend the Physician's Oath, and how to supplement and amend its provisions, all methods will be discussed and decided by the next Executive Committee, and compliance will be notified. (9) Wu Jishun proposed to protect medical rights. Resolution: Approved in principle. The method will be discussed and handled by the next Executive Committee. (10) Xie Yunshou moved to solicit members to revitalize the association's affairs. Resolution: Approved in principle. The method will be discussed and handled by the next Executive Committee. (11) Shen Mengyang moved that the association send a letter to the New Pharmaceutical Industry Association, stating that various injectable medicines should not be sold at retail without a doctor's handwritten signature and certificate. Resolution: A letter of advice will be sent, requesting compliance with the various regulations on drug management promulgated by the former Ministry of Health, Ministry of Interior, and Health Administration. After the motion was completed, the election began. As a result, Song Guobin, Yu Yunxiu, Wang Qizhang, Cai Yumen, Xia Shenchu, Xie Yunshou, Zhou Junchang, Tang Shouxian, Pang Jingzhou, Jiang Zhenxun, Guo Qiyuan, Liu Zhigang, Niu Huilin, You Pengxi, and Cheng Hanzhang, fifteen people were elected as executive committee members. Wu Yichu, Zhang Kecheng, Chen Zhuoren, Chen Rongzhang, and Diao Xinde were elected as alternate executives. Ye Zhisheng, Chu Minyi, Xu Naili, Niu Huisheng, and Zhu Qiluo, the above five people were elected as supervisory committee members. Wang Yugang and Ruan Shangcheng were elected as alternate supervisors. After the re-election, a dinner was held. During the dinner, Guo Qi, a member, was invited to give a speech (military medicine), and Comrade Mao Yun, a representative of the Municipal Party Department, was invited to give guidance. Finally, the chairman expressed acceptance of the guidance and gave a thank-you speech, announcing the adjournment.

Gu Kenfu Practices Law

Mr. Gu Kenfu was one of the earliest initiators of Chinese-made films. Many of the older film stars graduated from his school. His directed films, such as "Human Heart" and "The Door of Justice," etc., were all able to use artistic techniques to create extraordinary and noble works. He occasionally wrote articles and published them in newspapers and magazines. His arguments were insightful, clear, and fluent, and were widely circulated at home and abroad. In the summer of 1929, he served as the editor of the art column of this newspaper and published ten special issues on art. His words and style were regarded as the best in Jilin at the time. Mr. Gu graduated from the Nanjing Prison School in the early years of the Republic of China, so he is proficient in law. When the National Revolutionary Army established its capital in Nanjing, Mr. Gu drafted a film promotion plan and visited Hu Zhantang, Ye Chucang, Chen Guofu, and other gentlemen, who praised him greatly. Unfortunately, due to economic difficulties at the time, it was not realized. Dr. He Shizhen, the younger brother of Dr. He Shimei, the former President of the Shanghai Concession Temporary Court, admired his talent and extended an invitation to assist him. All documents and files that passed through Mr. Gu's hands were praised. At the same time, Mr. Gu devoted himself to studying law at the Shanghai College of Political Science and Law, which was run by Dr. Zheng Yuxiu, to seek further education. His performance was excellent, and he always ranked at the top of the examinations. The Shanghai Municipal Party Department and the Shanghai Municipal Government successively appointed him as a member of the Film Review Committee. The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau also appointed him as an editor and a social affairs investigation committee member. The film review rules formulated by the former Shanghai Municipal Film Censorship Committee were mostly derived from Mr. Gu's hand. Now, Mr. Gu graduated from the Shanghai College of Political Science and Law this summer and obtained a Bachelor of Laws degree. He has joined the Shanghai Bar Association and, starting today, will practice as a lawyer in various courts in this city and the Jiangsu Higher Court, the Capital Supreme Court, and other regions. The law firm is located at Room 4, Huiluo Building, 106 Sichuan Road, this city. Mr. Zhang Baichun has been hired as the Director of General Affairs, Jia Licheng as the Director of Accounting, and Mr. Li Boqin as an assistant.

Exhibition of Recent Works by Modern Famous Painters

▲Starts on the 13th

In recent years, painting exhibitions in Shanghai have sprung up like mushrooms after the rain, and the painting style is very popular. However, they are all collaborations by individuals or a small number of people, and there has never been a grand exhibition that brings together the best works of first-class masters. Now, reliable news has been received that Shanghai painters are planning to collaborate on an exhibition of recent works. The person in charge is Mr. Xue Baolun. Those invited by Mr. Xue to join include Wang Shizi, Wang Geshi, Wang Ziyuan, Jiang Xiaojian, Li Zuhan, Li Qiujun, Wang Shengyuan, Fang Huqing, Sun Xueni, Ma Qizhou, Ma Mengrong, Ma Wanli, Chen Xiaodie, Shang Shengbo, Fu Tienian, Zhang Shanzi, Zhang Daqian, Zhang Hongwei, Zhang Shimin, Xu Zhengbai, He Tianjian, Lu Xiaoman, Fei Longding, Huang Su'an, Huang Binhong, Huang Xiaoting, Huang Ainong, Ye Weishen, Yu Danhan, Zhao Shuju, Xiong Songquan, Zheng Wuchang, Zheng Manqing, Pan Tianshou, Liu Haisu, Zhu Wennyun, Lou Xinhu, Qian Shoushi, Xie Gongzhan, Yan Ganyuan, and other forty people. The works exhibited this time are all the proud works of the masters. Those who usually want to obtain their paintings but cannot easily do so can take this opportunity to choose at will. It is truly a rare opportunity. It is now scheduled to be exhibited at the Ningbo Fellow Association for three days starting on the 13th of this month. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

Reactions to the Demolition of Houses in Qingyun Lane, Tiantong Road

The tenants of Qingyun Lane, Tiantong Road, Beisichuan Road, Hongkou, Shanghai, received a letter from the lawyer representing the landlord Guangchanglong on October 30th, requesting them to move out within one month by the end of November of this year. Therefore, they gathered together to plead, and held a general meeting of all tenants at Yuanji Shantang. More than 300 people attended, elected a temporary chairman, and elected 21 executive committee members on the spot to discuss countermeasures. (1) Decided not to move out and require a satisfactory extension of the original deadline. (2) Six representatives were publicly elected to meet with the landlord. (3) Each tenant will raise funds for negotiation expenses. (4) Organize a temporary meeting place, located at 126 Qingyun Lane, to handle all matters. (5) Send letters to various groups for fair assistance. (6) Financial management will be carried out by the 21 committee members, who will elect a custodian. (7) All tenants should maintain a calm attitude. (8) Important news will be notified by the committee members at any time, and a general discussion meeting will be held. (9) Adjournment.

The Best-Selling Domestic Camel Hair from China's Only Factory

The Shuanglu brand pure wool, plain-colored, wide and tight camel hair produced by China's only camel hair textile factory on Niuzhuang Road is made from high-quality wool purchased from the Northwest, spun and woven by itself. The products are of excellent quality and reasonably priced, and have long been recognized by society. It is heard that since the beginning of autumn this year, various woolen fabric stores have been placing orders with it. The factory has been processing and rushing to produce day and night, but there are still too many customers who come to buy every day.

Letters to the Editor

To the Editor:

I am writing in response to the article in your newspaper on the 4th of this month, in the local section, regarding Cheng Chunlin, also known as Yi Kun, which contained slanderous remarks. According to the company, namely the American-owned Sino-American Silver Company, it had already been established long ago. I only submitted my application through proper procedures on August 5th and was assigned to work as a clerk and translator (taking small notes and translating) under a Westerner, Mr. Li Yaoguang (Mr. Li does not understand Chinese). All the employees in the company were there before me, which is known to all colleagues in the company. Moreover, my boss, Mr. Li, is just an employee and has no right to interfere with the company's business, let alone his translator and note-taker. Now, your newspaper has groundlessly accused him, which is deeply regrettable. I hope you will immediately investigate and correct the matter to avoid being falsely accused. Yours sincerely, Cheng Chunlin, also known as Yi Kun, November 8th.

To the Editor of Shenbao:

I am writing to express my shock and surprise upon reading the list of union representatives who went to 29 Gordon Road, Wu's residence, to petition, as published in your newspaper on the 9th, which included the name of the Nanyang Company Employees' Comrades Association. The Nanyang Company Employees' Comrades Association had a labor dispute some years ago and was voluntarily dissolved by all our workers. Currently, all our workers are well-treated by the management and the factory regulations are excellent, so we do not want to form any organization, nor do we have any representatives active outside. The name "Nanyang Company Employees' Comrades Association" as published in your newspaper is completely inconsistent with the facts. I am writing this letter specifically to declare this and request that you publish this letter (in the Letters to the Editor column) to clarify the truth. Yours sincerely, All 5,000+ employees of Nanyang Company.

On the 4th of this month, your newspaper published a telegram from Jiangsu Province party members urging peace. At the end of the telegram, the names of Xu Shaolie and Yan Huading, etc., party members from Kunshan County, were listed. Shaolie and Huading were completely unaware of this telegram. We are writing to request that your newspaper promptly correct this to clarify the facts and rectify public opinion. Sincerely, Xu Shaolie and Yan Huading, party members from Kunshan County, Jiangsu Province, issued on November 8th, 1931.

To All Newspapers:

Yesterday, we read in your newspaper about the telegram from Jiangsu Province party members urging peace, which included the names Zhang Gang, Fan Jingda, and Xu Houfu, etc., party members from Chuansha County. We were shocked and surprised. We were not aware of this telegram beforehand, which clearly indicates that someone has fabricated names and included them. We are writing this letter specifically to correct this. Zhang Gang, Fan Jingda, and Xu Houfu, party members from Chuansha County, respectfully.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Yangtze River basin is cloudy and uncertain, with rain or fog. Gales are quite strong in this coastal area, due to a low pressure system passing and moving northeast. There are strong northwesterly winds in the Yellow Sea. Winds in the East China Sea are non-directional. The center of a hurricane in the Pacific Ocean moved to within 120 miles of the intersection of 13 degrees north latitude and 131 degrees east longitude at approximately 11:00 AM this morning, moving westward. The center of a hurricane in the China Sea moved to within 60 miles of the intersection of 18 degrees north latitude and 116 degrees east longitude at approximately 11:00 AM this morning. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 66.2 degrees and the lowest was 54.5 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 64.4 degrees and the lowest was 59.7 degrees.

Reader Correspondence

Save the Nation! The People Must Rise Up!

Yi Yin

Napoleon said, "I am not afraid in front of a million soldiers, but I am afraid in front of a million people. I am at a loss for what to do." It can be seen that the power of the people is extraordinary. However, our Chinese people, to put it politely, are a peace-loving nation. To put it bluntly, they are a weak and useless nation. If not, in this unprecedented national crisis of humiliation, how can we not hear the voices of the majority of the people? One reason, of course, is that the people do not have sufficient knowledge. Another reason is that those patriots who shout for salvation refuse to go to the ranks of the common people. Therefore, the national salvation work that is booming in big cities is something that the rural people do not know what is going on. Our country is based on agriculture, and most of the people are scattered in the poor and remote villages. They are like sleeping in a drum. They are people who have not directly suffered pain, and they are still living their lives of "working at sunrise and resting at sunset." Therefore, if we want to have the strength to resist Japan and save the country, the first thing we must do is to go to the ranks of the common people to awaken them. Napoleon said, "There is a giant in the northeast. He is sleeping now, but do not wake him up. If he wakes up, he will become as strong as a lion." It can be seen that our people, once everyone wakes up, will not only make Japan fear, but also make all countries in the world fear. Therefore, awakening the people is the most important thing for future prosperity. The second is to lead the people. Now, the people are not all knowledgeable, so those who are more knowledgeable should be responsible for leading the people, telling them how to save the country, and walking on the same reasonable path. The third is to unite the people. Outsiders say that our nation is like scattered sand, but we must avoid this problem in the future and turn the 400 million scattered sand into a large stone, then our strength will be enough to apply. The first element of nation-building is the people, so to ensure the existence of the country, we must not forget the people at any time and in any place. I believe that only when the people rise up themselves can we avenge our hatred. If we rely on others, we will inevitably be trapped in a deep and inextricable position. Compatriots, rise up! Only when we rise up ourselves can we break our chains.

Social News

Foch's War Diary of the French General in the European War

— Translated by Gu Angruo

What was the situation on the east side of the Meuse River?

From October 8th to 10th, the French 17th Regiment, with the support of two American divisions (33rd and 29th), fought along the right bank of the Meuse River, while the main force of the American army attacked on the left bank. After fierce battles, they advanced to the Sivry-Buzancy line. After that, the American offensive encountered stubborn resistance from the enemy, and they felt that their forces were insufficient to defeat the enemy. The enemy seemed determined to hold the right bank of the Meuse River firmly, as this was the only way to cover the retreat of the defeated armies on the right flank and in the center.

In order to break the enemy's plan, the Allied Commander-in-Chief decided to advance towards Luxembourg along both banks of the Moselle River, and at the same time fight along both banks of the Saar River.

On October 20th, I sent the following instructions to Commander Pétain:

The current operational plan focuses on repelling the enemy to the area below Stenay on the Meuse River. To break through the enemy's defensive line on the Meuse River, preparations must be made to advance towards Luxembourg and the Saar River on both the east and west sides of the Moselle River.

Of the enemy forces guarding the defense line, there are 127 divisions west of the Meuse River, but no more than 32 divisions east of the Meuse River. Therefore, the speed of victory after the offensive depends on the speed of the deployment.

After the enemy loses the main transverse railway line from Metz to Sedan, our victory will be even more assured. Therefore, the French troops withdrawn after the shortening of our front line should be immediately sent to the Lorraine front on both sides of the Moselle River, because our strength and terrain in that area are conducive to a swift battle.

The deployment and participation of the American troops advancing on the left bank of the Meuse River should also be studied.

The Intelligence Department of the French General Headquarters detected that the German forces on both sides of Attigny were not evenly distributed. Once the railway line between Hirson and Mézières is lost, the German High Command will have no hope of restoring this balance. Therefore, we have more reason to decide to attack in the Moselle area. This offensive is not a surprise attack, as the enemy has been stationed in this area for a long time and knows that we will eventually attack sooner or later.

I had already discussed this with the commander of the German Eighth Army (General Chraulde) on September 20th. Commander Pétain had also notified Commander Castelnau a month ago to arrange for the group army headquarters to launch a joint attack.

On October 21st, the French Commander-in-Chief sent me the plan for the general offensive in the Lorraine area. This plan was generally correct, but there were some problems with its swift implementation, especially the operational plan west of the Moselle River, which failed to take advantage of the enemy's weaknesses to seize the opportunity for a quick battle. The situation east of the Moselle River was slightly better. I decided to immediately deploy all available forces to fight in that area first.

I temporarily abandoned the plan to attack Luxembourg and limited the scope of the original plan. However, from a military standpoint, I still wanted to use a small force to break through the defense zone that the enemy had established for four years. More importantly, from a spiritual standpoint, I wanted to be the first to enter enemy territory.

I asked Commander Pétain to prepare to attack towards Saint-Avold and Saarbrücken. On October 25th, he reported to me that the offensive would begin around November 15th. He also explained the source of the large forces required.

On the 27th, he designated the attacking units and the objectives of the attack for General Castelnau, the commander of the Eastern Army Group. The forces responsible for the attack were the Eighth (Commander Chraulde) and Tenth (Commander Michaud) Corps. The Eighth Corps had already been deployed to the front line, and the Tenth Corps had to move east from the Aisne River line and be positioned between the American Second Corps and the French Eighth Corps. The combat troops consisted of twenty infantry divisions (including four or five American divisions), ten to twelve field artillery regiments, one hundred and eighty to two hundred heavy artillery pieces, three light tank regiments, two medium tank companies, one cavalry regiment, and one air squadron. Commander Pétain stated in the military order that this was not a relentless direct attack on the enemy's defensive line, but rather a tactic.

The French Commander-in-Chief wanted several American divisions under his command. The American Second Corps was designated to protect Metz, (unfinished)

Youth Garden

Little Host

— Gao Sang

││The one who wins is Jinan beating Northenburg││

The school's sports department posted a notice that the football team would be playing Northenburg today. When two heroes meet, there will inevitably be a fierce battle.

Therefore, no one wanted to listen to the lectures in the classroom. Although our school is the base camp of the iron football team, we rarely see their achievements on the field on weekdays. Once the formal battle begins, we will naturally be especially eager. You invite me, I invite you, and the whole school is in great tension.

Under such a tense mood, Mr. Wang insisted on being a little host with me. Mr. Wang is a semi-fan. He said that Jinan is unreliable, who is sick, who is not studying, and seven out of ten are bound to lose. I didn't care, the victory or defeat will eventually have a result. Because Mr. Wang made such a prediction, I simply returned him with disbelief, and even said that Jinan will definitely win. Thus, the dispute began, and the two-mao bet was settled. We also asked Mr. Zhou to witness, so as not to be lazy afterwards.

The agreement was made in the morning, and the game was in the afternoon. For the sake of two mao, I earned a lot of warnings from Mr. Zhou. He said that if anyone lost and didn't pay up, he would definitely use force to resolve it, with the air of the League of Nations artillery. But he was also too unfair, just as if he was saying to me, "Is Jinan definitely going to lose?" I thought so in my heart, hoping that Jinan would win and retaliate against them.

Sure enough, the afternoon arrived, but we still had to attend classes. Carrying several pounds of foreign books, we inevitably had to be refined. Walking into the classroom, I saw that the students all looked impatient, but the time had not yet arrived, and they were unwilling to sacrifice themselves in vain. Mr. Pang came, silence, take notes. This year, I missed classes due to anti-Japanese activities, so I hurried to catch up. My pen was writing on the paper, but today I missed a lot. One sentence passed, I couldn't catch up. I looked at the classmate next to me to see if he had taken notes, but as soon as I looked, another sentence passed. So I had to let it go. The more I took notes, the worse it became.

Fortunately, class was over. Two mao was a small matter, but I didn't want to be angry. I didn't even have time to send the books to my room, so I ran to the field. There were too many people and I couldn't squeeze in. After turning half a circle, Mr. Wang and Mr. Zhou were occupying a stool in the left corner, leaving a seat for me, I thought it was for the sake of two mao. So I was very happy to get a commanding position. Mr. Zhou and Mr. Wang looked at me, inevitably getting angry again.

The north wind was blowing, the leaves were rustling. The wind behind me was blowing very hard, and fallen leaves flew onto my hair from time to time. The heads were crowded, and the Boy Scouts were blocking left and right, quite like the so-called "helping the scene" in playing tricks. Every time a bus arrived, the fans rushed desperately, like mountains and seas overturning, or like the north wind rolling fallen leaves.

It started. Northenburg was the British Royal Army, and everyone was tall and mighty, with an air of arrogance. Jinan, known as the iron army, had warriors of mixed yellow and black colors, short and lean, with the spirit of the Far East. As you came and I went, the white army gradually turned red, and the yellow army gradually turned white. The struggle was fierce.

Jinan was kicking against the wind, and the ball was naturally always in the backfield. The secret struggle between Mr. Wang, Mr. Zhou, and me was temporarily suspended. We stretched our necks and each had our own ideas.

Unexpectedly, a ball was shot towards Jinan's goal. The goalkeeper did not resist, but gently brushed the ball, as if saying something sarcastic. The ball honestly and politely entered the goal. So the whole field sighed. Mr. Wang and Mr. Zhou were the same, but when we looked at each other, they smiled slightly. I understood their thoughts.

It came again. Northenburg's goal was also broken by Jinan. The whole field cheered. Mr. Wang and Mr. Zhou were the same, but when we looked at each other, they smiled slightly. I understood their thoughts.

In this way, Jinan's goal was repeatedly opened, three to one. The white army defeated the yellow army, and the first half ended. The whole field was dim.

Mr. Wang's artillery was fired. He thought that the two mao were securely in hand, so he discussed with Mr. Zhou how to enjoy it. Mr. Zhou said to sit in the West Garden, a pack of melon seeds, two cups of coffee, just enough. Mr. Wang agreed, first declaring that the loser could not participate. I ignored them. The money was in my pocket, anyway, if they used force, I would run away. It was already a matter of course. At the same time, the game was not over, and it was difficult for them to issue an ultimatum immediately.

Ten minutes passed in a flash. Jinan's players rushed to the windward side to prepare to avenge their shame. The north wind was howling again, and the air was tense.

General Da Gai shot one into the British army. We smiled at each other. General Da Gai shot two into the British army. We smiled at each other. At this point, I thought that no one would win the two mao. In my joy, I formally gave them a blank stare. Mr. Zhou said, "Mr. Gao can rest assured, and there is no need to run away." I said, "Who is running?" "Can't afford to lose two mao?" This is a hard line of duty.

General Da Gai finally shot in the third one. The whole field roared like thunder. Mr. Wang threw Mr. Zhou's hat into the air to celebrate. But I caught it smoothly and stuffed it into my bag. The condition was there, but at that time the game was not over, and the situation was constantly changing. Mr. Zhou negotiated with Mr. Wang, asking why he threw his hat. Mr. Wang asked me for it, and I first said "Two mao for a small foreign coin".

It was over. A burst of welcome, the fans rushed back to the school, rushing to the outside of the school. Although Jinan's players were wounded, they were smiling and went home to change clothes.

The north wind did not continue to blow. Mr. Zhou's bald head became hairy. He urgently needed a hat. But I didn't give it. Mr. Wang was silent, admitting defeat. Finally, Mr. Zhou asked him for the two mao, but he didn't give it to me. The condition was to share the blessings. Mr. Zhou straightened his hair. Mr. Wang talked about today's football experience. They went to the West Garden together, three cups of coffee. They couldn't eat the melon seeds, so they each ate a small piece of beef. Because of the mess in his hair, although I returned the hat to him, he still demanded compensation for the loss. I said, "You are eating for free, just like the League of Nations."

Two Classes

— Jin

The first class in the afternoon was the troublesome chemistry class. The chemistry teacher was a middle-aged man with heart disease and rheumatism. When he came to class, he slowly walked out of the teacher's room, almost staggering with every step. Looking at his appearance, he seemed to have lung disease. He walked into the classroom, coughed a few times, and then weakly put down the roll book. His two pale and listless eyes glanced around, and then he raised his voice to call the roll.

It's really funny. Today, no one was listening quietly. It happened that there was no experiment, so there was even less interest. The students in the classroom were all doing their own work, like a self-study room. Some people even used it as a dormitory. The teacher was sitting upright in his chair and lecturing, but he didn't care how noisy we were.

Finally, the bell rang to end the class. The teacher took his book and roll book and slowly walked out of the classroom.

○ ○ ○

The next class was trigonometry. Mr. Hong hurriedly ran into the classroom. He was somewhat short-sighted and extremely sensitive to sound. He didn't allow us to talk, and he didn't allow us to look at other people's papers. If he saw someone talking, he would tear up their paper. When everyone heard this, they made faces at each other, not even daring to make a sound. At first, the teacher walked back and forth, monitoring us as if afraid that we would cheat. Later, he sat down casually, and then the cheating began.

Yun, sitting in the third row, coughed a few times to Juan, sitting in the fifth row, and then raised her thumb and shook it a few times. Juan understood her meaning and nodded, crumpled up her finished draft paper, glanced at the teacher, made a face at him, and then quickly threw it to Yun.

This class was really quiet. The teacher quietly sat in his chair and read the newspaper. We were also very quiet, not saying a word, but there were continuous coughs, as if everyone had caught a temporary cold.

Before an hour had passed, the papers had been handed in. Everyone jumped out of the classroom laughing and joking, leaving only the teacher in the classroom sorting the scattered papers on the desk. Then he hurriedly rushed out of the classroom.
